[1] The tenant of Room 13
[2] In Y-machi (of course in Tokyo), there is a building called Kanto Building, which looks modest in size. The building is currently on the market for rent. One morning, a gentleman of good appearance enters the building's office, and the receptionist takes his business card, which reads "Art dealer, Inoue Hiroshi."
[3] Inoue leans on a sturdy bamboo cane and fiddles with the silver chain hanging from his white vest, speaking haughtily:
[4] "If there's an empty room, I want to rent one."
[5] Kanto Building is in a prime location and has low rent, making it very popular. However, for some unknown reason, one of the offices has been unable to rent out. The owner is superstitious and believes that the number 13 is too unlucky, even considering skipping the number and adjusting all the room numbers. When this proud gentleman arrives, only Room 13 is vacant.
[6] "Room 13," Inoue mutters, grinning strangely. "Room 13 is fine. So, I'll have my luggage brought in today." He opens his bulging wallet and pays the deposit and one month's rent on the spot.
[7] The building is not a government institution, so it does not investigate the identity of the tenant, does not require a copy of the household register, and does not even require a guarantor. As long as one appears respectable and can afford the rent, anyone, regardless of their name, can rent a room at any time. Of course, "Zhang San Li Si" is not Inoue, but even if the "art dealer Inoue Hiroshi" business card is fake, as long as no one suspects it, no one will question or verify it.
[8] After receiving the rent and deposit receipt, Inoue leaves the office and heads to a nearby public phone booth (4).
[9] "Hello, K Furniture Store? This is Inoue from Room 13 of Kanto Building. I need to buy some things urgently, and I would like to see the ordered items as soon as possible. Please select and send them over. I need a desk, a swivel chair, three ordinary chairs, and a large display shelf. I'll pay you right away when the items arrive. I don't mind if you use the display items in your store."
[10] After calling K Furniture Store, he continues to call G Art Gallery, S Framing Store, and other places, placing orders for all the decorative items needed for the newly rented office. It seems that Inoue is an odd art dealer who orders from art galleries and framing stores he has never had business with before. It's hard to tell how much profit he makes from such a business. There are indeed some strange businessmen in the world.
[11] By around 2 pm that day, Room 13 of Guandong Building had been decorated to look like a respectable and stylish art gallery. At first glance, it could be considered a respectable and stylish art gallery. The 10-square-meter indoor space was hung with large and small oil paintings and prints, and a glass-enclosed display cabinet in the corner housed busts, partial sculptures of hands or feet, and various clay pots. The other corner was filled with white canvases and frames.
[12] In the center of the room, there was a large desk, and a few chairs were placed around it in an orderly manner. The new owner of Room 13, Rice Yuan, sat heavily in the swivel chair behind the desk and began to write vigorously on the memo pad in front of him. He looked as if he had been working here for a year.
[13] To give the reader a sensory impression, I would like to introduce Rice's style here, but to be honest, he doesn't have any special style. At most, it's just that Rice has a big, curly mustache that doesn't look like a businessman, and there's a triangular goatee on his chin that looks a little fake. However, this hairstyle was rare at the time, and it made the tall, slender 40-year-old Rice look quite like a British gentleman, with an added touch of aristocratic dignity. He has a long, narrow face, is almost thin enough to see his bones, has a pale complexion, and has very thick hair that is well-groomed. Compared to his face, the large tortoiseshell-framed glasses seemed a bit out of place.
[14] As for his clothes, he wore a thin black gabardine jacket with a white cotton vest, and paired it with a gabardine stripe pants, with a low-key style that suited him well.
[15] While the elegant Rice was writing, there was a knock at the door, and someone had come to visit.
[16] "Come in."
[17] Inoue responded in a crisp, low voice, and the visitor timidly pushed open the door. A surprising young girl's face peeked through the crack.
[18] "Come in."
[19] He said it again, and the girl entered. She stopped at the spot between the door and the desk, fidgeting. She wore a light-colored crepe kimono with a red floral sash, and although she was not particularly beautiful, she seemed quite introverted.
[20] Inoue immediately showed signs of impatience, beckoning her to approach the desk. The girl walked forward a few steps, fidgeting again, and then took a small piece of paper from her sash.
[21] "Well, I came because I saw the morning newspaper."
[22] She gently placed the piece of paper on the corner of the desk.
[23] The piece of paper, actually cut from the three-line advertisement column of the newspaper, read as follows:
[24] Seeking a female clerk, 17 or 18 years old, charming and likable, responsible for greeting art clientele. Excellent pay, afternoon three to five o'clock at the store for interviews.
[25] Yachimachi Kanto Building Inoue Artware Store
[26] It seemed that Inagawa had placed the newspaper ad before renting the apartment. Did he know in advance that the 13th floor of Kantou Building was vacant? This person's actions were quite peculiar. Did he purchase the goods from other retail merchants in the art industry or order them automatically via a telephone? He advertised for a secretary before even renting an office, and everything was unconventional. However, this might be the business method of the times.
[27] Meanwhile, Inagawa looked up and down at the girl who came to apply for the job, and finally said in an unapologetic manner:
[28] "I'm sorry, but we have already found the person we were looking for in the newspaper."
[29] As readers know, the girl was the first visitor to the apartment after Inagawa moved in, and yet he said he had already found an employee. What an odd response! How bizarre could this person's methods get?
[30] The empty mansion
[31] Nioyama's store was thriving from the moment it opened, and from then until 5 o'clock, there were customers at the door. However, the visitors were not customers, but all came to apply for the position of female secretary. But Nioyama was still happy, as if he was enjoying a pleasant task, patiently repeating the same answer to each young girl who came to visit:
[32] "I'm sorry, but the person we advertised for has already been found."

[34] The girl's age was about seventeen or eighteen, as required in the advertisement, wearing a lively and colorful dress, a low hat covering her eyes, and stockings reflecting a shimmering light.
[35] Nioyama's eyes, hidden behind round glasses, squinted as he looked at the girl standing straight in front of the desk. His gaze seemed to lick her whole body.
[36] The girl in front of him was petite, with muscles that were quite firm, but gave the impression of being soft and malleable, as if she would become soft and pliable if hugged gently. Her skin was a healthy tan, her puppy-like eyes were shy and twinkling, her lips were slightly upturned, like a petal, her nose was short, and she was a very distinctive girl.
[37] After a long look, Rice Field finally said something different from the repeated lines.
[38] "What is your name?"
[39] "My name is Rizuki Hanabi."
[40] The girl not only did not shy away, but even exuded a seductive pose. Rice Field's eyes narrowed even more behind his glasses.
[41] "My store has very few staff, so although you are responsible for greeting customers, you actually have to do a lot of things. For example, organizing goods, keeping accounts, and taking on the role of a secretary, and so on. Is that okay with you? However, I will pay you weekly, 15 yen (5) a week. Can you accept such conditions?"
[42] "Yes, that's fine. As long as you think I can handle it, I can do anything."
[43] "So, do your parents agree? Did you say you were going to come here today?"
[44] "No, I haven't told my family yet. When I left home today, I only said I was going to a friend's place. However, if they know I've been hired by your store, I think they will be very happy too, because they have been encouraging me to find a job."
[45] Upon hearing this, Rice's small eyes flashed with a glint, staring straight at Fangzhi. For some unknown reason, he seemed to emphasize something, asking the same question again:
[46] "Do you think your family knows you came here today? Have you mentioned it to any other friends?"
[47] "No, I haven't said anything to anyone. It would be embarrassing if they knew I wasn't hired."
[48] "Good, then I'll hire you today. However –"
[49] He glanced at the clock as he spoke.
[50] "Oh, it's already 5 o'clock. My store usually closes at 5, even though it's already past closing time today. But I still want to show you the location of my house and let you see the inventory in the warehouse. So if it's convenient for you, can you come with me now? Don't worry, it's not far, and we'll take a car, so you'll definitely make it home in time for dinner."
[51] "Uh…" Lijian Fangzhi was still hesitant, but she felt that the store owner, both in age and character, seemed trustworthy, so she mustered up the courage to answer:
[52] "Sure, I'll go with you."
[53] "Then, you can go out first, and I'll think about it. Please wait for me at the crosswalk across the street. I'll come over once I finish cleaning up here."
[54] In reality, there was nothing to clean up, but Li Yunquan used this excuse to send Fangzhi out first.
[55] Meanwhile, Fangzhi was so happy to find a good job that she didn't notice anything odd. However, Li Yunquan's actions became even stranger, although they were nothing compared to what came next.
[56] Fangzhi arrived at the crossroads he specified, and soon a car slid in front of her.
[57] "Miss Li Xian, come on, get in the car quickly."
[58] Fangzhi saw that Liang Yun was indeed sitting in the car. Although she found his actions puzzling, at that moment she had no time to think, so she got in the car.
[59] The car drove east from Y town for a while and stopped when it reached S town near the Two Nations Bridge. Liang Yun said:
[60] "I have some business with a client, and I can also introduce you to them." He let Fangzhi get out of the car, told the driver to leave, and then walked into a narrow alley nearby. After a few steps, he suddenly remembered something and hurriedly explained:
[61] "Oh, I almost forgot, the client went on a trip and is not at home. I'm so stupid today."
[62] After turning a few corners in the complicated alley, he came to a major road and hailed another car. This time he had the car go west, driving about twice the distance of the original journey before finally stopping at R Town in the Yamacho district. They left the office at five o'clock, and after going to find the client, they had wasted a lot of time, so the streetlights on both sides were already lit up.
[63] "I'm sorry for the delay, but we'll be there soon."
[64] Nao dismissed the car driver and walked into a deserted alley next to R Town. The two sides were endless walls, and this should be a quiet residential area. There were almost no people on the road, and the streetlights were sparse, so walking inside felt like walking into a huge, dark cave.
[65] "If I don't go back, my family will be worried..."
[66] It was clear that Fujimori was an adventurous woman, but for some reason, she suddenly felt a little scared, standing in front of the alleyway that felt like a cave.
[67] "We're almost there, just about half a chō (6) away. Even if you go back now, you won't be too late. Since you're already here, why not take a look?"
[68] Regardless of her willingness, Nioyama strode ahead. Miss Fujimori, most of the time, underestimated things and, when faced with obstacles, would just go ahead and take the risk. Tonight, her mood was in the middle, with two completely different ideas tugging at each other, but her slightly aroused curiosity managed to take the upper hand, and she followed the man in his forties with a somewhat Western touch.
[69] Indeed, after walking less than half a chō, a tasteful courtyard appeared between two mansions, of medium size. There was no light at the entrance, and it was too dark to see the address. The sound of a sliding door creaking could be heard in the darkness, and Nioyama had already pushed open the sliding door and walked into a pitch-black courtyard.
[70] "My wife may have gone out. This guy is so careless that he didn't even lock the door."
[71] Nioyasama mutters as he fumbles around in the dark, and then the porch lights up.
[72] About a room (7) away from the main gate is the porch's sliding door. The two paper doors at the other end light up, and Nioyasama stands in the porch about three tatami mats big, beckoning to Fuyu.
[73] Fuyu is surprised by the owner's shabby appearance. Does Nioyasama's wife not lock the door when she goes out, just like the women in the big courtyard? Moreover, there seems to be no maid at home, and the owner has to turn on the porch light himself when he comes back. Will he be able to pay the salary?
[74] After being brought into an eight-tatami-mat-sized inner room and sitting on the floor without any cushions, Fuyu's heart is no longer just uneasy, but surging with an inexplicable fear. This house that Nioyasama called his private house should not be an empty house, right? Fuyu's gaze sweeps over every corner of the house. There are neither cabinets nor tables, no wooden sandals at the porch entrance, and the alcove in the living room is empty. There are neither hanging scrolls nor any ornaments. This is too strange. It seems that what he said about his wife going out is definitely a lie to children.
[75] "You seem very afraid," Nioyasama looks at the restless Fuyu, his heart seems to be sneering, his tone is strange, "Actually, this is not my house, just an empty house. I took off the lock beforehand. As for the lights, I also prepared them myself, and I can turn them on at any time. Are you afraid? But now that you're here, you probably won't want to scream or run away, right? But even if you scream, it won't work. All around are mansions, huge and hard to imagine. This is a secluded, standalone courtyard. I locked the door from the inside just now. Even if you want to escape, with your delicate arms, you probably won't be able to escape. Understood? You are smart and should know what to do and what attitude is most favorable to you in this situation. I am a bad guy, a bad seed. If you resist me in this situation where you are at a disadvantage, you will fall right into my trap. You understand that, right? So, you might as well still treat me as the owner of Nioyasama Art Gallery, treat yourself as the new female clerk who just applied today, and this is the owner's house. Let's not argue or turn against each other and waste time, and let's have a pleasant conversation, how about it?"
[76] Fujiko's lips turned pale when she heard this, but before Oshino noticed, she swallowed her fear and embarrassment. Although she was still trembling with fear in her heart, at least she could now show a calm and composed expression on the surface. She said calmly:
[77] "But why do we have to come to this strange empty house?"
[78] "Good question. You're smart, so I can breathe a sigh of relief now. You mean, why choose this empty house instead of going to a coffee shop or a hotel? You can ask directly... However, I chose a secluded house for a special reason. You'll know the reason soon."
[79] Oshino maintained his gentlemanly demeanor, as if he were chatting with a friend, and his tone was quite calm. It seemed that he knew that any violent words would be more terrifying than this attitude and make people more afraid.
[80] Bath Tub Spider
[81] "I invited you to see my warehouse, but unfortunately, this empty house doesn't have one. So, I plan to show you something else, which is the bathroom. Although this house is a bit small, the bathroom is large and impressive."

[83] Fangzhi was not the kind of woman who disregarded chastity, but despite knowing that in this situation, ordinary girls would take what attitude and action, she had already come to terms with the fact that no matter how hard she resisted, it would not change anything. She didn't have the rigid purity of ancient women, so she felt that it was better to face it calmly rather than struggling against it. She calmly thought about it and looked at the small suitcase."

All of this was for you. Until now, I didn't know whether you were Fangzhi Miss or whoever, I didn't know your name or appearance. [121] Little demon
[122] Why did the art dealer, Inagawa Hiroshi, bring Fangzhi into the bathroom where even the bathwater had not been heated? [123] Putting aside this point, three days after the bathroom incident, the newspaper published another three-line advertisement. As before, the advertiser was Inagawa, and the content was still bizarre. What strange trick will this eccentric gentleman play this time?
[124] Seeking a salesperson, regardless of eloquence, methods, and education, only seeking honest and reliable single men, with a monthly salary of 100 yen, plus transportation expenses, and face-to-face interviews.
[125] Inagawa Art Gallery, Ytown, Kanto Building
[126] At first glance, it looks like an ordinary job advertisement, but upon closer inspection, it seems a bit off. Education can be accepted, but hiring a salesman without requiring eloquence and means is too strange. An introverted honest person would never be able to handle the job of a salesman, and these hiring conditions are completely against common sense. Moreover, it requires "single young men," which is even more puzzling. Regardless of the employer, they would prefer to hire a trustworthy married person, but this job advertisement goes against the norm in this regard. Moreover, in addition to a monthly salary of 100 yuan, it also provides transportation expenses, which is too good for a novice.
[127] Since the qualifications of eloquence, means, and education are not required, any impoverished young man would be eager to apply. On the day the newspaper advertisement was published, there were a hundred applicants rushing to the East Tohoku Building.
[128] Kusaka only went to work on the day he rented room 13 (the day he brought Fujiko into the empty house), and since then until the day the newspaper advertisement was published, the store has been locked and he has not appeared. Today, in order to select the applicants, he came to the store early and sat in the swivel chair behind the large table, as if he were a modern art gallery owner.
[129] On the display cabinet next to him, in addition to the plaster statues bought before, he also brought several plaster models of human body parts commonly used by painting students using his car today. (So, does Kusaka Art Gallery have a warehouse for storing plaster statues?)
[130] The oil paintings hanging on the wall, the high piles of picture frames piled up in the corners of the room, and the furnishings in the room are still the same as before. The gold paint on the picture frames glitters, and in the early summer sunlight, it is extremely dazzling.
[131] As for Rice, he was still the same, smilingly bringing in groups of applicants for interviews. His calm demeanor makes one wonder if the ruthless Rice who was like a poisonous spider that night is the same person. A criminal who is excellent at acting.
[132] After nearly half a day, six qualified candidates were selected. However, Rice's recruitment examination was unusual. All the energetic, optimistic, and business-minded young people - the kind of young people that general interviewers would definitely hire - failed. On the other hand, those who only nodded their heads when asked, didn't know how to answer, were not familiar with the world, were shy and introverted, and were as old as a cow, were green and pale twenty-year-olds, passed smoothly. He recruited six of them. In other words, Rice selected the most useless and inept young people from a hundred applicants.
[133] After selecting the qualified candidates, Mr. Rice instructed the six to stand in front of the table and gave the following strange orders:
[134] "Everyone has seen, this is a store that sells oil paintings, picture frames, and plaster statues. Among them, selling human body plaster models, which are a must in painting courses, to art schools, middle schools, and girls' schools, is the main business of this store. Look at the works displayed on this cabinet, they are quite good, right? Your job is to take a sample of a plaster model and sell it to various middle schools and girls' schools in the city. Although it is a sales job, it is actually a gift of the product to the other party, using the probative pre-gift to make the other party feel good, and then slowly expanding the true meaning of sales, this is my business strategy. So it is not difficult at the beginning, as long as you make the other party happily accept the plaster statue. In the future, I will also ask you to sell them to various prefectures and cities, but for now, we will start from the city.

[153] The expert in limb crime
[154] Now, let's learn about another main character in the story - Dr. Panan. In other words, we will tell the story of the odd Mr. Inagawa, the little demon Mr. Hirata, and the five salesmen from another angle.

[156] Dr. Pankin is considered Japan's Sherlock Holmes, a part-time detective and amateur crime scholar, but he is not a half-professional detective like Sherlock Holmes who takes on any case (11). He only takes on cases that interest him and only suggests to the police when they encounter difficult cases, so only those in the legal and law enforcement system know him, and he is not well-known in society. He only takes on cases that interest him, does not receive visitors, but once he takes on a case, he can definitely solve it, and Dr. Pankin himself has an unusual personality, which can be said to be identical to Sherlock Holmes in the novel.
[157] The reason why it is said to be unusual is that Dr. Pankin, although he is a medical doctor and a renowned expert in criminology, does not teach or hold any official position. He lives a reclusive life, secluded in his study, and does not socialize with anyone, immersed in books all day long, and is a rather reclusive person. However, once a rare criminal incident occurs, he becomes active and engages in paper reasoning, and sometimes even takes risks and ventures into the vortex of crime cases despite his physical disability.
[158] Dr. Pankin is a disabled person who has lost one leg. A few years ago, he had a railway accident and had his leg completely amputated from the thigh, and now he has a prosthetic limb. Although he does not need a cane and can walk with a regular walking stick, he still looks limping. Perhaps Dr. Pankin's reclusive life is because he is ashamed to show his ugly posture to others. Moreover, Dr. Pankin has never taken off his prosthetic limb in front of anyone. When he needs to take a bath, he only bathes in his own locked bathroom, and he must not have a very ugly incision.
[159] In terms of appearance, he is tall, and other than his leg disability, he has a few similarities with Sherlock Holmes. Although he is slightly balding, his long hair is casually scattered on his shoulders, his thin and elongated face, his smooth chin, his serious and thick eyebrows, his sharp eyes, his long and straight nose, and his thin lips form a "one" shape, all of which are identical to the British detective, and he exudes a cold calmness and a sharp wisdom. As for age, Dr. Pankin claims to be 36 years old, but he looks a bit older at first glance.
[160] Sitting opposite Dr. Pankin, his assistant Norio, a 24-year-old handsome young man, is an avid reader of foreign detective novels and has even set a goal to become an amateur detective. Finally, three months ago, he admired Dr. Pankin's fame and became his disciple. He has become an indispensable chat partner for the lonely Dr. Pankin. Although he has a poet's temperament, he is very intelligent and sharp-witted, and sometimes even says surprising things that make Dr. Pankin surprised.
[161] The study is decorated in a Western style, leaning towards the classical style favored by the doctor, with a high ceiling and imposing wood carvings. The entire room exudes an eerie atmosphere. The walls of the room are lined with custom-made bookshelves, with long shelves reaching up to the ceiling. Ancient books are arranged in rows, revealing gold lettering on their spines. In the center of the room stands a large desk with intricate carvings, upon which a doctor in a suit has his elbows resting on a mirror-like surface. His freshly shaven cheeks are reflected in the glossy tabletop as he gazes at a spread-out clipping in front of him:
[162] "Everyone knows that most news reports are just nonsense and should not be taken at face value. However, do you know why I took the trouble to clip and save these reports? When it comes to news reports, it's all about how you read them. Sometimes you can read between the lines and uncover hidden information. Especially in the field of crime, you could say that all the secrets of the world are hidden in the words of news reports. My reading style is slightly different from the norm, and I am familiar with the writing habits of reporters from different newspapers. I can tell which reporter wrote which article in which newspaper. Based on their writing style, I can also infer the subtle details that were not printed. Therefore, if a crime occurs and different newspapers publish different reports, even ones that contradict each other, that is where my interest lies and where the most important information can be found. By comparing the usual personality of the reporter - what kind of events they often report on and what kind of errors they make - with the differences in reporting from other newspapers (this method can be applied to any report), analyzing, deducing, and drawing conclusions, one can unravel the truth of the matter. In fact, I have found crucial clues to solving major cases just by comparing news reports on my desk. This is not out of curiosity, but because it is an indispensable tool for my detective work."
[163] Dr. Pianyu is like a friendly teacher, warmly imparting his years of detective secrets to his disciple, Yasugi. This attitude, which the eccentric doctor has never shown to anyone else, is an exception.
[164] "There are also interesting advertisements in the newspaper, especially the three-line advertisements in the recruitment column (12), which often hide unexpected crimes. At least, you can find five to six strange advertisements in the content every day. From the three-line recruitment content, imagine them as complex social issues, love problems, or even criminal problems, and reconstruct different plot stories. Even if you just treat it as a game, it is endlessly interesting. Well, instead of just talking about it, let me give you an example. Here is a clipping book of three-line recruitment advertisements, with several recent advertisements pasted on it, some of which are quite interesting. Take a look."

[473] "What? A forged letter? You mean my daughter, Hina, has been taken by bad people too?"
[474] "It's possible. Anyway, I have to go back. Leaving you here alone might be lonely, but I'll send someone from the house to come over soon. Please bear with it for a moment."
[475] Nakagawa left the old lady, bidding her farewell, and rushed back to the doctor's house on a taxi.

[477] "What is it?"

[487] "The Mermaid of the Aquarium (17)"
[488] After Dr. Banken, Yasuzaki, and Detective Waga met at the Inagawa residence in Shiba, they conducted a thorough search of the area, but found nothing. The demon, like a free-roaming ghost, left no trace except for the letter - the only clue - not even a hair.
[489] However, the next day after Miss Hinoki's disappearance, another incident occurred that shocked the readers of Tokyo's newspapers.
[490] From the southern coast of Tsu, walk across a long wooden bridge to the island of Izu. At the entrance, you will find a small aquarium. Although it is still early for the summer vacation, most of the visitors to the aquarium are tourists from out of town, and the empty indoor space looks like a quiet tourist attraction in the off-season, especially in the morning, where there are almost no customers. Only the ticketing clerk and the elderly janitor can be seen yawning and chatting leisurely.
[491] At around 10 o'clock, a visitor finally bought the first ticket of the day, a young oil painter who came to sketch. After handing the ticket to the gatekeeper at the entrance, he walked into the dim and quiet gallery.
[492] The interior is dimly lit, and the water tank, which is about the width of a room, is lined up on both sides like a showcase. The indoor lighting shines through the dark blue water and the thick glass board, making the interior look like the bottom of the sea, cool and cold.
[493] The young painter leaned his face against the glass and observed one by one.
[494] Some of the tanks have a group of giant spiders, the mantis shrimp, crawling weirdly among the dark rocks; some tanks have giant octopuses, their eight legs firmly attached to the glass, their disgusting suction cups clearly visible; the square pufferfish, like an irritable and strict country old man, dashing left and right; the colorful stonefish, like a seductive dancer, spreading its huge body and swimming leisurely; and rare sea snakes, twisting their phosphorescent bodies and dancing wildly.
[495] However, what's going on? The young painter walked to another tank and jumped back a step, then cautiously approached the glass board, bent down, and peered into the upper half of the tank with his hesitant and wandering gaze. What kind of strange fish is moored there?
[496] Gradually, the young painter's face turned increasingly pale, until his entire expression froze.
[497] "Mermaid, mermaid…"
[498] He waved his hands frantically, as if trying to shake off some phantom, his almost fainting body swaying violently, and then he let out a loud scream, stumbling out of the gallery in a frenzied rush.
[499] At the entrance, the old man with the tudou pipe (18) was leisurely puffing away. The young painter grabbed his sleeve and dragged him to the tank without a word, leaving the old man bewildered and unable to protest.
[500] "Look at that! Look at that!"
[501] The young man forcefully pushed the old man's face to the glass edge, his voice panicked and dry, incoherent.
[502] Initially, the old man had not yet recovered from his anger and confusion, but when he accidentally glanced at the sink, he also let out a sharp scream and jumped back, just like the young painter.
[503] Floating on the surface of the water was an object, a giant mermaid lying on her back, drifting helplessly in the water.
[504] Her black hair was like tangled seaweed, her lowered face did not lose any of its beauty even with the furrowed brow of pain; her full breasts hung in the water, like petrified stalactites; her legs, crammed into the narrow sink, twisted into an unusual curve. There was a huge wound under her left breast, slowly bleeding out and slightly staining the deep blue water in the sink with blood.
[505] At the sight of such an incredible scene, neither the young painter nor the ticket old man realized that a terrible murder had taken place, nor did they react for a moment that it was a victim's corpse. However, readers must have guessed that the mermaid in the sink was the beautiful corpse of the victim, Rikko Hijiri, who had been cruelly murdered by the evil demon.
[506]The third victim
[507]In the second murder case, the killer left no trace. It was only known that the victim was the older sister of the victim of the first murder case, Fujiko, who was tricked into going somewhere the day before she was killed by someone impersonating Dr. Panko. Her heart was cut out with a knife, and the autopsy determined that she died around midnight the previous night. There were no other clues for investigation.
[508]In addition, a fisherman living in Pizay told Detective Hori a clue on the day of the incident.
[509]The night before, he stayed at a friend's house until around two o'clock, and when he passed under the long bridge connecting Pizay and Jima Island, two shadowy figures appeared on the bridge, hurrying towards Jima Island. The fisherman was startled, seeing two vague silhouettes in the dark night, which looked like two men in suits carrying a large bag.
[510]Investigation revealed that no one in the surrounding area carried anything over the bridge at that time that night.
[511] Based on the above insufficient information, the following crime scenario is inferred:
[512] The killer probably took the victim to the empty house where Hanae was killed (No. 19) and killed her cruelly after achieving his purpose. He then put the body in a bag and drove to Nagisa along the highway, arriving at the long bridge where the car could not be driven. At that time, the killer and his accomplice carried the bag to the aquarium and removed the glass cover above the water tank, throwing the body into the tank. The victim's time of death was around midnight, and the killer arrived at the long bridge around two o'clock in the morning. Therefore, the two hours in between were equivalent to the driving time from Tokyo to Nagisa.
[513] Dr. Pankan received a call from Detective Waga and went to the scene, where he could only admire the killer's clean and efficient crime scene and find no clues.

This shows that the killer had a preference for the appearance of the victims, causing great panic among young women.

[619] July 5th

[632] Killing is an art. Even without quoting de Quincey (27), I am deeply convinced of this. Young and beautiful women are my artistic subjects. [1236] Injured Hakuba Doctor
[1237] In this story, the author did not describe the commotion caused by the incident in society, as he dislikes redundancy. [2148] In the blue and red alternating light, the spider man's face was smiling like a demon, and laughter from the bottom of hell flowed out of his open mouth.
[2149] Panorama Hall is located at the corner of the amusement park, with separate entrances and exits. Even if you don't enter the park, you can visit Panorama Hall. This free entrance has become his secret passage for transporting a huge number of victims.

[2152] He held a thin whip and walked into a room that looked like a storage room but was actually a darkroom.

Under the threat of the whip and gun, they had no choice but to choose to enter the dark, narrow tunnel-like hole leading to the Panorama Pavilion.
[2154] The scene was really ridiculous. The naked women were driven like a herd of cattle, one after another, into the Panorama Pavilion hall.

[2160] An extremely strange situation occurred in the dark storage room where the forty-nine dolls were kept.
[2161] A doll lying in the corner - a shamble of a large man's body wrapped in a loose white lab coat and a woman's head grafted on - one of the many imposters. Suddenly, it rose from the darkness, pushing aside the pile of dummies and walking along the wall.

The spider man's soft body collapsed between the mannequin's arms, and the anesthetic drug put the demon to sleep.

[2169] "Ah, I was just so happy that I got dizzy. Nothing."

What happened in that hour and who the strange mannequin was, the answer would soon be revealed.
[2171] These things will not be discussed in detail for now. Spider man, Kita Daizou, stumbled to his feet, and he continued to whip and roar to make all the girls stand in the right position. The forty-nine girls cried and yelled again, but this time they surprisingly obeyed his orders.

The Pannoramic Hall was laid bare, and the naked limbs of forty-nine women were visible. In the blue and red intertwined light, they twisted and turned.
[2174] Spider man let out a wild laugh like a beast, his face flushed with excitement, and he licked his lips, very happy to press the small button on the wall of the small room. After pressing it, he pressed his face against the glass of the circular window and watched the changes in the scene.
[2175] The button was connected to the poison gas device set in the floor of the audience's seats. As soon as it was touched, the two drugs inside would automatically mix.
[2176] Soon, in the darkness below the audience's stand, countless yellow smoke snakes stick their heads out one after another. They crawl on the ground, spreading in all directions, overlapping and intertwining with each other, and finally becoming a yellow smoke wave that slowly approaches the forty-nine naked women.
[2177] The girls frightened by the poison smoke let out screams and huddled on the backdrop. However, the poisonous snakes quickly approached their feet, climbing up their ankles, calves, thighs, buttocks, abdomens, along their skin, and they danced the spider man's so-called crazy dance.
[2178] This is a tragic battle between forty-nine soft bodies and poison gas. The girls coughed violently from the smoke, but their terrified hands couldn't hold back their screams from their chests, and their drunken dance lost its rhythm and turned into a frenzied dance. The spectacular scene of forty-nine naked bodies running back and forth, intertwining, delighted the spider man to the extreme.
[2179] The yellow smoke became thicker and covered the ground and the circular backdrop, finally climbing up the circular ceiling and escaping through the ventilation holes outside. The glass window where the spider man peeped was also covered by the mist, and he could no longer see the whole scene inside. However, when the numerous naked women running wildly rushed past the peep hole, the huge bodies in the smoke were magnified several times, like giants in the clouds or strange fish in an aquarium, lewd and terrifying.
[2180] However, even the spider man could not enjoy this incredible sight for too long. The yellow poison smoke invaded through the gaps in the walls and began to invade the small room where he hid. Knowing the properties of this poison gas, he was already trembling with fear just by seeing a wisp of smoke. He quickly took a handkerchief to cover his nose and ran out of the small room, ran through the corridor to the outside of the Panorama Pavilion. He closed the entrance door tightly and fled from the building in fear, running at full speed into the forest on the other side.
[2181] For the spider man, who has escaped from the clutches of the sleep demon solely by willpower, this frantic run finally exhausts all his strength. When he collapses in the forest, lying on the grass, the partially ineffective anesthetic drug once again takes control of his nerves.
[2182] He lies there, looking up at the Panorama Museum building. Under the pale sky, the dark, circular building rises, with yellow smoke rising from its roof. Ah, under the circular roof, forty-nine twisted bodies lie on the ground, vividly showing their desperate struggles before death. Thinking of this, he feels both satisfied and sad. His neck, which had been raised, falls limply, and this rare demon finally falls into a deep sleep.

No, no, no, it was impossible for such a ridiculous thing to happen.
